RATING: 9
[COLOR=#FFFFFF][BGCOLOR=#FF9933][b]aaj's FAVORITE REALTIME GAME[/b][/BGCOLOR][/COLOR]
New players can pick this game up very quickly, and defeated players are always hungry for another chance to defeat the temple. Once we've won the base games, there's alternate soundtracks, curses and treasures, Queenies, and expansions to throw in the mix. 

I honestly can't see myself (or my game group) growing tired of this game because Queen provides so much control in adjusting the difficulty of the temple. With the exception of teaching newbies (which remains difficult because they aren't used to the game), no rounds are ever ho-hum for me.

Some folks have grown tired of the game around on the forums, but playing one or two rounds a month has kept it pretty fresh in our group. It's definitely long-lasting, and the expansions go even further than the base game in keeping it fresh. 

I have run into some trouble when playing this game with other people -- due to my wife and I playing it two-player so often, we're [I]very[/I] experienced in the temple and we can often be bored by a temple that others consider to be quite difficult! We get around this by either handicapping ourselves in some way or by sitting out of the game and managing it (selecting the different quests to tune the difficulty, etc). Overall, that's just a disappointing wrinkle on a great game.

Escape was one of the first games I bought, and the basic idea of a timed game with a soundtrack and real-time dice rolling will never get old to me. That said, the game isn't without its flaws, though it's still a venerated favorite in my collection.

RATING: 7.5
As far as I saw, I tend to like real-time games more in theory than when I'm actually playing them at the table. The frenzy of going against a clock makes in fact this kind of games quite exciting while you are playing them, but more often than not I unfortunately leave the table with a strange feeling of dissatisfaction. I don't know if it's because these games are so light or because I expect more from them, but I don't seem to be able to particularly enjoy them. For the most part Escape makes no exception to this rule.

Yet I really like this game. It has clearly many strengths: the production quality is very high, the game is easy to teach and play, it's very fast, it's cooperative and it's quite exciting while you're playing.

I wasn't happy with some elements of its game-play though. For one thing the game seems pretty easy to win and that usually isn't something you want from a cooperative game, because the frustration resulting from the losses is very important to build up to the moment you actually beat the game and cheer. However this might not be necessarily a flaw, if you're looking for a more family friendly experience. What bothers me more it's the repetitiveness of the game-play. It's not just the fact that you're basically rolling dice for 10 minutes, but more that the game plays out the same way every time: explore the temple, remove crystals, find the exit.

Fortunately both of these problems were solved by the many expansions that the game has. In particular I think that the Doomed expansion brings a good deal of variety, thanks to the treasures and the curses, and a new level of challenge to the game. It makes it for a considerably better experience.

So, summing up, "Escape: The Curse of the Temple" is a pretty good product as a filler and a game to play with family. It deserves its success without a doubt. Personally though, I feel the game needs to be played with the expansions in order to satisfy my personal gaming taste. Still pretty nice though! Very good game.

Rating without expansions: 6.5

RATING: 5
In this game you have to explore a dungeon, collect as many gems as you can, and exit, and do all of this in exactly 10 minutes. The mechanics are simple: you roll dice and execute the rolled icons. It is cooperative, as you win only if all players have exited. It is fast and funny, a good partygame.

RATING: 9
A real-time game done right. Simple rules for quick decision making that is just fun to play.

The game is very thematic; the time pressure and intensity you experience as you play makes you actually feel like you are in a collapsing temple needing to make quick decisions. You also feel a sense of camaraderie as you work together with the other players.

The only downside is that if the dice actually go your way and you work well together, the game can actually be too easy and a little anticlimatic. In a way, you kind of hope things don't completely go your way so that you can enjoy it even more when all of you make it out of the temple with seconds to spare.

RATING: 7
Quick playing games are hard to find and frequently suffer from lackluster play.  This title is fast enough to hit multiple plays or can be the perfect filler for a longer game day.  The game play is very straight forward.  Its easy for players to start out without cooperation (and ultimately lose), but with a little cooperation and individual play, a team of players can beat the game without too much challenge.  This could be a problem, except that there are able ways to ratchet up the complexity of the challenges and should result in the game play being able to stand up to repeated plays.  This is not a gamer's game, but it is fairly novel in its design (or at least in limited company) and it really shines as a express filler.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
1 to 5 players. This game is fun, but it's extremely simple, you simply have to roll dice as fast as you can and work your way through.
It's a real time game, so no turns or rounds, and certainly no A.P.!
Standard level is very easy, you should use the expert level (+3 gems) most of the times.
It can get very tense as players have to work against time.
The cooperation works quite well where you sometimes have to go through some tiles to help another player that got stuck. The best strategy for the players is to stick together and go for the tiles that allow to activate 3 gems.
The basic game comes with 2 extra modules, the treasures and curses. While the curses are drawn as soon as you discover a cursed tile, the treasures are put on the drawn temple tile and later you have to roll 2 keys to pick it up.
Probably best wih 3 or 4 players.

This game really needs expansions, because the game only comes with a very simple expansion. And the base game is way to simple for repeated plays, it's only good for introducing new players.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.75
The tension!! As much as I love a good thinky Euro, I really have a deep love of the adrenaline rush of this dice chucker. It's push your luck while under the intense pressure of a realtime time limit. There is so much variety to add with the various expansions, that the game really scales well for newcomers and veterans alike. I'll usually get 2-4 games in a row, adding in various modules with each go. My favorite is using base game, plus illusion tiles with the special rooms, and throwing in characters and quests. Then maybe I'll throw some curses and treasures in for good measure.

RATING: 7.5

…But, it REALLY should have included the illusions expansion. The base game just feels incomplete. There is a definitely lack of variety.  After one hour of play we were ready for something new.

Revised: As suspected, the expansions (specifically, the second expansion: Quests) add challenge and variety to the game.

RATING: 7
"Haha, that's a fun easy game. Well, too easy. Look I have 2 crystals and another. Is this supposed to be hard? Wow look the first time I ever get a black mask no match for my golden ones. Oh OH! QUICK I WENT FULLY BLACK AND I NEED A GOLDEN MASK! HELP ME!"

RATING: 9
Really fun - a bit surprised to see my geekbuddies are not huge fans of this. What's up with that, gerkbuddies? You are usually pretty reliable. Don't make me come over there! For a 10 minute game of frantically rolling dice, there is also a surprising amount of strategy in how to explore and how to balance the risks and rewards of spreading out.

The only downside here is that the base game alone is not *quite* challenging enough once you get some experience, and the expansion situation is a bit out of control. Lots of mini-adds, some are good, some are not. I think the Traps expansion is actually the best. The curses are good but the iconography is not always great and the last thing you need is to have to go to a reference sheet in a timed game. Keep the set of curses small and comprehensible, don't just throw stuff in there. In general just add a couple small things to the game each time. This is not something you're going to play so much that you're going to master all this stuff.

I should also mention, for gamers, the Zombie City version of this is better - more dynamic, more thematic, more challenging, more interesting, more attractive, better mini-expansions, but also slightly more complicated.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Escape is a very innovative and fast-paced real time cooperative game.  Players are explorers trying to escape a tomb, and must frantically roll dice to overcome the obstacles that the tomb presents.

Dice must be rolled in order to run into adjacent rooms, discover new rooms, and complete challenges which will eventually make it easier to escape the tomb.  For example, one room might require you to roll 7 torch symbols.  This is problematic since each player only has 5 dice!  Thus, teamwork is required since it is much easier to obtain 7 torches amongst two or three players.

There is one die face that, when rolled, curses that die and makes it unusable until the curse is removed via another certain die symbol.  Sometimes, via very unlucky rolling, a player can become stuck, and another player must rush in to save that player by rolling the curse removal symbol for him.

There are no turns in Escape.  Rather, everyone is continuously rolling dice the entire game, trying to complete everything as quickly as possible.

Eventually, the explorers must find the exit and escape!  The players must complete all of this in 10 minutes, or the tomb collapses and the players meet an unfortunate ending.  This creates a very tense game, where players are playing at a frantic pace the entire game, while also working as a team as best as possible.  A team that is too slow or does not cooperate well will find themselves trying to do better next time!  If a team masters the tomb, there are additional components that may be added for additional difficulty!

RATING: 7
Fun, but stressful, real-time game in which players need to escape from a temple by rolling dice for 10 minutes and hoping for the best. Definitely chaotic since every player rolls their own dice (as opposed to a common dice pool like in Fuse) and rewards good communication between players, especially when some get stuck with locked, cursed dice. Obviously not a super strategic game, but a really nice filler or a great way to start a game night before jumping into heavier fare.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.15
This game is an absolute blast.  It packs tons of fun into a 10 minute experience.  The real-time chaos is exciting and never lets you go.

So, with all this praise, why is my rating not higher?  I'm a tad worried with the longevity of the game as it proved rather easy for us (4 players using the Curses/Treasures modules).  The book does offer certain tips to add difficulty but I wish there was a more interesting official way to scale the game besides just adding more gems.

I also don't think you could play this game every week multiple times as it would start to become dull.  It's not terribly deep (although strategy does help) and is more about the experience.  It's like riding a roller coast - if you ride the same coaster 50 times in a row the 50th time is not going to be as fun as the 1st.  Now if you space those 50 times out across a couple years, then you can retain the excitement longer.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A relatively mindless game of rolling dice as quickly as possible. Which is fun in spurts of a few games, but I'm not going to play it for an hour straight. The game improves with the addition of the expansions, giving you a little more to process while you play, and becomes special with the addition of the challenges, giving a sense of growth to the game.

The biggest problem with this game is that it is so unforgiving to the less experienced players of the group. Even playing just the base game without the expansions they are often overwhelmed as they try to keep up with everyone else resulting in just doing what everyone else is doing and not really making their own decisions.

The second biggest problem is that while the game is very light to play (few decisions) it is very difficult to explain. There are a lot of rules to remember (for a ten minute game), and once you have experience, it is really only fun if played with lots of expansions. But, you can't just throw them all in, so you have to separate and sort, remember how to do set up, then remember what each mini expansion does, which is a whole bunch more rules. Now, in many coöps, rules are less of a problem because if someone forgets a rule, you can simply discuss it and it doesn't create a problem as it does in competitive games. However, in this real time game, you might need to pause the timer every minute or two while someone looks up what a particular curse does or a quest or a treasure. And that's after you just spent ten minutes explaining it all. For a ten minute game.

Much like Space Alert, I think this game is best with a dedicated group of players who are going to play it frequently enough that they can remember all the rules. It is fun, but without that group, probably more time used outside of playing than time having fun playing.

RATING: 7

Play with the "silent" soundtrack - it's clearer when something is happening AND less annoying.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
[b]Copy includes the promo #1 Escape: The Pit and #2 Escape: Doomed.[/b]

Escape is a wonderfully approachable real-time cooperative game where everyone is trying to escape the temple before it collapses and must roll dice combinations to move from tile to tile and place gems onto tiles. It's fast, frantic and all done to a soundtrack that times everything.

The game is flat-out fun. I can teach relative non-gamers how to play, but even "serious" gamers should find enjoyment in this if they approach it with the right spirit. The game comes with a second tile set of curses/treasures already in the box, so even though it's a 10 minute game, there's variety built in, which helps ease seeing that sticker shock on a 10 minute filler.

A possible knock? The game has been relatively easy to beat, but that's remedied by ramping up the gems you need to place beyond what the rules state. I haven't yet played this with the full complement of five, but I imagine the more the merrier to create an added amount of chaos and group dysfunction!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.25
If I had to pick one word to characterise this game, it would be FUN. It is hectic and loud and just fantastic. Components are of excellent quality.

If you are the kind of person who can't be a little silly, then DON'T play this game. If you (and the people you're playing with) throw yourselves into the game, you'll have the best time. There'll be lots of shouting, working together, laughing, etc. Each time we've played, everyone wants to play again.

(TIP: When we play as a group we put the soundtrack through an amp and dim the lights to make it more thematic)

This isn't a very "thinky" game - it's 10 minutes long! But I think with multiple plays you come up with strategies to increase your chances of winning, so it definitely isn't mindless.

I think this game would appeal to a variety of ages (I've only played with adults) though it is probably too stressful (with the time limit) for young children.

There is one caveat to my glowing review though: the price. I don't know what it sells for elsewhere, but in NZ it costs $90 NZD (about $70 USD), which feels like a lot for a game that lasts 10 minutes. This put me off getting the game for a long time. It IS worth it, but somehow I feel like it should market for slightly less because of the short duration of a single game. If it were cheaper, I could see it becoming a mass-market classic.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
I always preface these reviews with the fact that I'm not the target audience for these games and basically play them only at cons and only for the benefit of sitting down with people who I enjoy gaming with.

Escape is a dice rolling co-op game. Players explore a temple using 5 dice which govern their ability to move and get rid of the cursed treasure that is preventing them from escaping. The play is completely free-form, you roll and roll and roll trying to get the correct dice to move or match the requirements for whatever room tile you're currently in. Dice can become locked on a black mask side and getting them unlocked requires the use of a gold mask (another side of the dice) by either yourself or your team-mates.

The main issue I see with this design is that there is no penalty for keeping all of the players together at all times and in a larger group this makes it pretty easy to fill each of the treasure tiles quickly and also largely negates the threat of black masks locking up dice. I played it twice and we were owned initially by splitting into 2 groups and by not paying attention to a timed requirement to get back to the entrance to avoid losing dice (bad for obvious reasons). The second play we stuck together and defeated the game pretty easily even though we were not efficient with time in the middle portion of the game and still lost some of our dice in the first. In short, after two plays I don't think there is anything else to see here. That said, it's 10 minutes. That said again, people might insist on playing the soundtrack instead of just using a nice, quiet sand timer. Shrug.

RATING: 3

Plus it all needs to be done hurryhuryhurry lest the CD proclaims they are out of time and doomed to stay in the temple forever. The atmosphere is frantic, and everyone is psyched. RATING: 9
Phenominal experience.  10 minutes of your time spent screaming, shouting, rolling dice as fast as you can trying to get out of a temple-OMG THE GONG I NEED TO GET BACK TO THE CENTRE HELP ME GET THIS DICE!...

On top of the simple game that is very easy to get into, you can add more stuff into the mix to make it more and more complicated: treasures, curses, weird illusions, a chalice, player character powers, a ghost(?), more curses, and those traps that I haven't gotten yet...WHAT? It is bonkers the amount of game you can get out of it. Emotionally draining after every game, but it' the most efficient usage of 10 minutes in your lives. or 30 minutes, depending on how much time you spend explaining or playing again.

I really like this one. Try it at least once if you can.

RATING: 7
When I heard how Escape works, I thought, "Not for me."  I'd played Space Alert a few times, and decided the intense time pressure and shouting involved wouldn't work for us.  But then my husband surprised me by saying he wanted it as a gift, so I thought, "OK, why not."

And while the game is very intense, there's a simplicity to the rules which makes it easy to remember while you're under the gun with that timer.  A group that can play this multiple times will be rewarded by seeing themselves get closer and closer to that exit in time.  Fair warning: this game is possibly addictive!

So while this might not be for everyone, if you want a lighter game in the real-time genre, this might be for you.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
This is a fun game, but very chaotic. 

Escape is a cooperative game, you have exactly ten minutes to flee the temple and only if all the players have succesfully exited the temple, will you have won the game. So you win or lose together.

Each player has five dice to start with. If you throw a black mask with one or more of your dice, then these are deactivated until you throw a golden mask. If all your dice are deactivated, you can either wait for help or add a gem to the pile, which makes it more difficult to exit.

Everyone playes simultaneously, so you can help each other. Usually, there's a lot of shouting involved, as time is very short to find the various rooms, activate the gems and find the exit in time as every three minutes, you need to be back at the start tiles or lose one of your dice.

To add to the stress, the game comes with a CD with an Indiana Jones-like tune, but unless you turn it rather loud, players will probably overshout it :)

RATING: 6
Real-time games have a core problem that is very difficult to overcome.  When everyone is playing at the same time, who is checking to make sure the players are doing things correctly?  Escape is no different.  We won but we're pretty sure that we screwed up.  Not only is no one looking at what we do.  But we are pressed for time and more apt to make a mistake amidst the chaos.  How many torches do we have.  I think it is 10, get 3 gems.  Wait, 2 of the torches we counted aren't in the room.  What, I was in the room but left.  No, you were in that room.  Whatever, the clock is ticking, move those gems!  Kind of funny in a non-game way.

I liked the game though, but this issue makes it teeter away from what I think is a game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Players are Indiana Jones type explorers, racing through a temple, trying to solve puzzles to unlock the exit, before it collapses.  Fun real time game, fixed at exactly 10 minutes in length.  Players play at their own pace, there are no turns.  Players roll their own set of five dice, and use the results to open up the temple by revealing large, chunky tiles.  To move into a tile requires a certain combination of results, and about half the tiles have a "puzzle" to solve - a result that must be rolled a certain number of times.  Solved puzzles are recorded by placing gems from a pool onto them.  Somewhere near the bottom of the stack of temple tiles is the exit - players must throw a number of "key" results equal or greater than the gems remaining in the pool to exit.  If all players make it out inside 10 minutes, it's a win, otherwise it's a loss.  

This is a fun game, played against a 10 minute soundtrack.  The free form nature of rolling and using dice works well.  The cooperation element is strong, as some tiles require two or more players to pool their dice results to fully solve the puzzles and drain the gems (thus making it easier to escape).  Additionally, the cursed die result typically requires players to help each other out with the gold "break the curse" result.  The two gongs that occur on the soundtrack, forcing players to return to the entrance tile inside a minute or lose a die, is a nice touch - adding a dash of chaos to the already frantic experience.  

Looking forwards to playing more of this, with Illusions, and Pits, and Curses, and Treasure!  Well done, Queen.  This one does get the blood pumping!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Played once without the curse cards to learn the game. It was a little underwhelming, but I hear that the curse cards are what really make the game.

You could say that's a problem with the player and not the game, but when we beat the game, I always wonder if we really beat it fair and square. RATING: 7
Frenetic, incredibly stressful, and thematic; what's not to love? It's a quick game that's guaranteed to take ten minutes or less, and everyone will be engaged the whole time*. It's a near-perfect icebreaker or gateway game for players willing to deal with the excitement and stress the game offers. The game forces players to work together through the black and gold masks, and there's constant communication and discussion and yelling and general fun.

There are a few quibbles that take the game from amazing to merely good, unfortunately. Staying together makes the game a bit easy and excessively dependent on the way rooms randomly come out. I much prefer splitting up; there's more tension and the game becomes more dependent on how quickly the players can get particular symbol combinations, which is the more fun part of the game. The soundtrack is a little unclear (I prefer playing with the timer), and the base game can be a little samey (and expansions complicate the game enough that new players don't do as well.)

*I've had one player who wasn't quite up for the game once, but it wasn't the game's fault. Board games were really Not His Thing.

RATING: 7
From a technical standpoint, I find pretty much no flaws with this game. It is well-designed, simple to explain, and most importantly, lots of fun.

At the same time, it is also a little repetitive. I appreciate that it comes with modules for added variety, but since playtime is so short, and since you are so likely to play several times in a row, it still doesn't take very long to figure out the path to success.

I think the key to making this one last is to pull it out sparingly, and with different groups, preferably with a lot of new players. Like any cooperative game, you'll enjoy it more if success remains uncommon.

RATING: 10
Never before in my life have my hands shaken while attempting to beat a board game...Until Escape:Curse of the Temple.  You and your fellow teammates have 10 minutes (timed by a soundtrack.) to get out of the temple. There are no turns. Just people with 5 dice attempting to roll their way out of a dungeon. The soundtrack isn't just pretty sounds letting you know time is up. Within the ten minutes there are two intervals where a gong sounds. You HAVE to race back to starting square before the door slams or you lose one of your 5 dice. believe me you NEED all of your dice to open new rooms, move in and out of them, and solve puzzles making your escape easier. 

I have seen sheer panic on my son's face as he is screaming for help to get out...It is an INTENSE game. Co-op and helping each other is highly encouraged because if all members do not get out...everyone loses. The game also is not overly hard or easy. I have won just as many games as I have lost.

RATING: 7
Escape is a frantic real-time game experience.  Another example of this type of game is Space Alert.  There are big differences between these two games however.  The biggest difference is how much easier Escape is to teach players than SA.  Escape also plays faster than SA.  SA is mainly driven by cards whereas Escape is driven by dice rolling.  I think there is a lot more variation from game-to-game in SA but Escape is easier to teach and faster to play, so it's going to hit the table a whole lot more.  Escape also seems to have better experiences in how well it plays within the listed player range than Space Alert (ie I think Escape is good with any number of people whereas SA is probably 4 or 5 player only.)  The bottom line is: if you've never played a frantic real-time game you should try Escape and see how you like it.  If you like it and you think you can get a dedicated group to play the more complex Space Alert regularly, you'll probably want to give that one a try.  I could see owning both in a collection.

Edit: I would now completely recommend Magic Maze over Escape, unless you really despise silent coops.

RATING: 6
(As of [b]1[/b] play) An interesting conundrum. I enjoy real-time co-ops like Space Alert, but this is, with a full complement of six players at least, almost [i]too[/i] real-time. Everybody is rolling frantically, splitting up, regrouping, and fun things are taking place, but there is no chance to register anything beyond what is happening on your own tile. Unlike Space Alert, there is no chance to lovingly relive everyone's mistakes and moments of glory without the time pressure. It's all silly and fast enough not to matter much, but I somehow feel like I'm missing part of the fun. Will have to try it again.

Round 1 [3:40 total]: 0:20 Start, 3:20 Gong, 04:00 Door close (heartbeats for final 10 seconds) 
Round 2 [3:00 total]: 4:00 Start, 6:20 Gong, 07:00 Door close
Round 3 [3:20 total]: 7:00 Start, 9:40 Gong, 10:20 Door close

Prototype Designers Cut:
Round 1 [4:00 total]: 0:00 Start, 3:12 Gong, 3:17 Warning, 3:57 Door close (countdown for final 10 seconds)
Round 2 [3:00 total]: 4:00 Start, 6:12 Gong, 6:17 Warning, 6:57 Door close
Round 3 [3:00 total]: 7:00 Start, 9:12 Gong, 9:17 Warning, 9:57 Door close

RATING: 9
Very intense and fun game! It is very easy to learn the game, yet in each play, there are enough randomness and strategic decisions to make.

While it is intended to be a fully coop game, my family decided to add a house rule: when we heard the last gong, the game turns into a save yourself race game, with each player tries to get out the temple and ignore the other players. The ones who get caught in the Temple lost, the first to exit win. It adds a lot of tension to the game!

RATING: 9
This game is REALLY fun. If you're looking for a game that's easy to teach, requires teamwork and cooperation, and is quick, this is the game for you.

It's light, but that's the beauty of it. The expansions and modules add more flavors that really spice up the gameplay. There are so many ways to play that I can't see this getting old any time soon. I've played over 20 games so far and I'm still raving about it.

RATING: 8
A very good, very unique, real-time dice-chucking fun as players cooperatively try to bust their way out of a collapsing temple.  The fact that it actually plays in 10 minutes with no scoring or post-game activities to work through is a plus.  This game demands repeated plays more than probably any other game in my collection.  Each game can start feeling samey when played at the basic level - once you've solved it once, there's less motivation to keep going and try again - but the game comes with a couple of additional modules that keep it from feeling permanently "solved".  The soundtrack is great (one of my 12-year-olds was genuinely a little creeped out).  I don't know if I've seen so many people I've introduced it to so taken with a game after their first play or two.

RATING: 5
While Escape is sort of related to Space Alert, it is a lot less demanding with its primary focus on (re)rolling the dice as quickly as possible. And while the cooperative element - you cvan share dice with fellow adventurers in the same room - is quite important (some of the more difficult tasks are impossible to achieve on your own, and it's easy to get stuck with a few unlucky rolls) it is not particularly engaging.

Escape is not exactly un-fun to play but despite being a very short game I don't feel compelled to play "just one more time." Maybe what I miss most is some sort of feeling of accomplishment after a successful escape from the temple.

RATING: 7
The luck-based nature of both the generation of the temple and rolling locked cursed dice is mitigated significantly by its cooperative nature. Ultimately on the simple side, but the balance of helping each other and trying to travel around the temple manages to entertain under its very short time limit.
The most pressing factor is how well the game kills the alpha-player problem through simply making the game real-time: Players cannot micro-manage each other without performing worse for themselves.

(64 plays)
First Impressions: 8

The game has begun to grow quite thin after 54 plays. That is roughly 9 hours of game time.

RATING: 6
Escape is a frantic 10-minute game of frenzied dice rolling and tense banter. I recommend that anyone who enjoys cooperative games should try this if they have the opportunity. I thought it was a lot of fun, but I don't think it would continue to be fun if played repeatedly. The simplicity and compactness that makes this work so well as a walk-up-and-play filler would become a weakness if the game saw heavy play by the same group. So I guess I view Escape as a novelty game. I'll be happy to play it, but would never buy it, especially at the exorbitant Queen Games price level. Talk one of your more profligate friends into buying it!

RATING: 7
1-6 Players.  This game is a major hit in all 3 of my different games groups.  It is a 10 minute "filler" game, but it usually gets played about 6 times in a row because everyone wants to play "just one more!" with added difficulty.

People are yelling, screaming for help with their black masks, laughing uncontrollably (when someone gets the "can not talk curse" and we heckle them to just tell us what they want and stop mumbling), rolling dice like mad, cursing when they can't get keys, and cheering and panting when the game ends.  It is a very high energy game.  I tell people to stretch out before the game starts so they don't pull something!  I can't wait for future expansions.

RATING: 7.5
Prev. Owned : Vendu (Gobelin)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.2
This is good as a family game. Not something I would play with my competitive gaming group. More strategy comes in to play as you load the depot up with more and more gems, or mix in curses. Our win rate is really high, but we have fun doing it. We are nearing 10 plays with no signs of the game getting stale.

Update: I took this over and played with a guy from my gaming group, and surprisingly it quickly became one of his favorites. Playing with him was much better for me as well. We managed to clear win a game with 15 gems in the depot (2 players) without curses, and as many as 12 with. I will note, however, that when we added the curses it became more difficult to win with 2 at higher numbers. We lost several times in the 10-12 gem range and you become much more vulnerable to bad dice rolls. Increasing my rating to 9.5. We are now at around 15 plays and the base game shows no sign of getting stale.

Update 2: Nearing 10 plays with my buddy from the gaming group (about 20 total) and we are becoming very proficient. Now having no problems knocking out 12 gems 2 player with curses. Will continue trying to find the right balance of difficulty and excitement. The game remains a good filler, we remarked yesterday that it is the best 10 minute game we have every played.  

Update 3: After 20 plays this one was losing steam. Mixed in the Illusions expansion and that freshened it right back up. If you love the game I would suggest adding that for more replay ability.

Update 4: Zombie 15 has taken over as our real time game of choice. This will stick around as it is still fun to break out every now and then, but we prefer almost everything about Zombie 15 more except setup time.

Update 5: This game has pulled back even with Zombie 15 on account of the fact that I can pull this out and start playing within minutes. It is much more random, but the setup time holds Zombie 15 down. Still fun for a quick filler.

RATING: 7
This is the game Space Alert should have been (though it's a much lighter game). It's probably the best real-time game I've ever played. It's amazing how well the game allows players to do their own thing while still helping each other out. Most cooperative games, real-time or not, don't manage this balance nearly so well.

The custom dice, large and chunky tiles, and oversized meeples all look and play great. The theme is instantly relatable and works very well with the feel of the game, all running around the temple and trying to help each other out for a few frantic minutes. 

Out of the box, it's probably a bit too easy, but this does make it very accessible for non-gamers and there are myriad options for increasing the difficulty. The price point is probably a bit high for what is essentially a filler, but the component quality is excellent, so it's forgivable. 

This is a game the succeeds perfectly at what it sets out to do. It's possible it could wear thin after many plays, but the thrills and teamwork this game offers are unlike any other. This one is a definite winner, even though it's not my favorite type of game.

RATING: 7
This dice-chuckin' co-op does what it means to in a frantic way, and it works nicely for what it is, though I can see why some copies are turning over as people burn out on it.

Basically, a whole lot of rapidly thrown luck is generated by a set of action dice. They can lock and unlock on their own, and there are a number of things you need them for to turn over temple tiles, unlock cursed gems, and try to get to the exit tile with enough keys before your 10 minutes is up.

It's fast, it's fairly frantic, and there is a lot of luck- some games it seems like you throw what you need, others you can't seem to roll a break, and end up with all black idols staring up at you.

Starting this at a 7, with room to move.  I don't think it hugely appeals to the family, so it's staying power may be tested here.

RATING: 9
Our go-to for two player games. We play with The Pit, Doomed, and the normal curses and treasures. Even as a teaching game, I don't think the game should ever be played without curses (if there's at least one person who knows the symbols). I've played this at higher counts, which is fun and chaotic, but it's a very focused at two. It's very good solo as well, but at all player counts, you must improvise ways of increasing the challenge over time (more crystals and the like). We also tried the sand timer once, but the audio track is important. We've started playing with Quests as well as the newer starting system devised by the designer. Quests is a fantastic addition to what already is a super replayable game. 

I ultimately traded it because after around 40-50 plays, I think I'm all set on how fast paced the game is (more a personality thing, but it says a lot that I still loved Escape so much!). I also didn't get to play Quests as much as I would have liked because it's just too much to juggle with new or intermittent players. Overall, I'm glad to have owned this for a few years, but I may wait a while to revisit the genre.

RATING: 8
If you have ten minutes to spare, Escape: Curse of the Temple gives you an experience like no other. I've introduced this game to so many people and it has gone over amazingly well. Each play of the game, even with just the base tiles, is unique and different enough to warrant tons of plays. But more has been added in the form of Cursed tiles and treasures that changes how certain things work, making for a harder or easier experience, and is great that it is included in the box.

Update: I ended up selling my copy (of the big box version) after over 30 play( I haven't logged all my plays on here) I still very much like the game, but it's a bit light even for a real-time game. I think Escape Zombie City may be more "gamey" than this one, and Zombie 15' was definitely a better real-time game, but that one really fails in the setup department. IF it hit the table I will definitely play, but a game like Project Elite would be a better real-time game with more meat.

RATING: 7.5
A great, quick game for a broad audience (from old to young, from seasoned to new players, etc.). Easy to learn, a blast to play, and the soundtrack makes it immersive right alongside teammates shouting in you ear with both panic and revelry.  I suggest an untimed playthrough at first to help orient new or young players to the rolling mechanics and to ward off unintentional or intentional cheating (that may emerge under the pressure of the clock). Gameplay is a delightfully frantic 10min but you'll likely want to play multiple times in one session. Really creates a co-op vibe, builds camaraderie, and fulfills that 'just plain fun' portion of the collection. Components are rugged, durable, and of high print quality... a very solid investment. I suggest buying the Big Box edition which includes additional expansions that give the game added dimension, value, and higher replayability.  ESCAPE!  ESCAPE NOW!  You won't be sorry.

RATING: 5
Pure Insanity! That is the best way to describe this game. From the moment the gong rings (yes...there is a gong) the room you're in will be deafened by the sound of dice slammed to the table as everyone is trying to roll as quickly and as often as possible!

This is one of the few games that I can say, "This will only take 10 minutes to play" and that's because....it literally takes 10 to play. This game is the filler of filler games.

Definitely play with the "curses and treasures" expansion that come with the base game. These make your experience hilarious since some curses forbid you to talk, play with one hand on your head, or penalize you for being to crazy with your dice rolling.

RATING: 8
Fast paced and frantic real-time dice rolling game, in which you are trying to move through a temple constructed from tiles and complete small "missions" on these tiles in order to escape.  The game is cooperative in the sense that you all win or all lose, and there is limited scope for sharing dice.

The time limit on this game is only 10 minutes, this is good for several reasons.  Firstly, it makes the game frantic (and loud, if there's a few of you playing!) which is very thematic and adds much needed tension to what is basically rolling dice.  Secondly, the game is so short that you'll want to play it several times every time you get it out, which is great as it gives you a few goes at beating it, other cooperative games often don't give you much reason to try them again if you lose.  Lastly, it makes it a very good game for newcomers to gaming, as you'll only waste a few minutes if people don't enjoy it.

All the components for this game are great - the dice are clear, the tiles thick and colourful, and you get some lovely green gems.  The game is dripping in theme and really helps it feel atmospheric with the soundtrack playing in the background.

Very highly recommended, especially for people who like to keep "gateway games" in their collection.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
So got in a few games and its everything its supposed to be and you think it is. Thematic, fast, fun, frantic filler that can be stressful (probably TOO much for some people, best part for us!) if you are really 'playing' the game (hurry, hurry! [The two midgame races back to the entrance coupled with the music REALLY add tension here) Its also pretty unique and the theme really shines through.   

I mean its a 10 minute dice rolling filler, so of course there aren't lots of juicy decisions to make, but note you wouldn't have TIME to make them if there were! Its really just a nice real-time co-op race against the clock, and I think it does it mostly right especially if you get the difficulty right and come 'close' to winning or just barely win which most of our games have been tense finishes(and difficulty is VERY easy to modify due to the design).  

Will be a big hit this Christmas with all the non-gaming people I know, and I'm sure I'll enjoy playing it with them too (note the wife rates it 9.5). Hard to say how long this enjoyment will last, I am thinking 30 maybe even 40 games, enough to make the rounds with it anyway (although its SO short, it could turn out to be more). Note that it already feels somewhat samey after 5 games, since all you do is roll and explore the same rooms, but for some reason it seems to matter less than many other games as I think you are just too caught up in the race and beating the game (and many people are reporting playing 40+ games and still wanting to play so its a shared effect I think) 

I'm thinking best with 4 but will scale pretty well to any number of players (including solo which I even tried first night I got it to take a quick run through it, first time I ever played a boardgame solo). Oh, yeah after playing I think the two person per tile 'rule' needs to be there

[u]Update[/u]: Played 2 more games, have now played 1,2&4 players, 4 was the most fun for sure with much more yelling and chaos, we played 2 people could only stay on a tile, so just split into two groups and it worked great. I'm tempted to up it to 8.5, I think its very near the same fun level as Space Alert, which I have as 9 but I do worry we will burn out on this one too quick if we don't shelf it for awhile after 15 or so plays. Note have not Escaped in 7 games (edit 10) which I think is a good thing (I also included curses from the start) as I love a good challenge and know many others do too. Here are a couple of my comments from SA that also apply here:  

[i]Like most co-ops group dependency will dictate how much fun you have, our whole group loved it and we played 6 times in our first night of discovery with this game. That says a lot coming from me anyway and I feel it has a great addictive quality where you want to play again to improve, take on harder challenges or just beat the ones you just lost. The game has a nice tension to it with needing to act "under the gun" and boy can things go to hell in a handbasket in a hurry if your not working together. [/i] 

[u]Update[/u] - Yep, 15 plays and the dazzle is lost, but note we did them in like 5 days so that part is our fault I think.  If you (can) keep plays to occasional it will go farther, but regardless I would like to see some more drastic changes (other than just curse or room) in an upcoming expansion to breathe some life back in this one

-----------

Beat the clock real-time co-op filler that plays in a guaranteed 10 minutes and has many tense finishes?  Sign me up. Sure its ultra light and dice rolling but damn 10 minutes flat has an appeal, especially for weeknights :zombie:  If you keep the difficulty up and you and your group 'get into' the game I can see this really getting the blood pumping...

From the great walk-through video that was made (watch it if you want to know EXACTLY how the games plays), I know this will likely be an 8 - 9 game for the wife and I and a hit with some of our 'non-gaming friends', another reason to have it (who are slowly becoming converted...bwahahaha)

Possible houserule - My friend M.Webb inspired - Only 2 (3?) players can 'stay' on one tile? Its pretty easy to see this being an issue, and I definitely don't want it being too easy so will likely play this way.  
[q=CortexBomb] The main issue I see with this design is that there is no penalty for keeping all of the players together at all times and in a larger group this makes it pretty easy to fill each of the treasure tiles quickly and also largely negates the threat of black masks locking up dice [/q]

RATING: 6.5
2013-01-22

Initial Rating: 6.0 (January 2013)

Fun familiar (loud) dice fest game. After hearing this had a soundtrack a la Space Alert, I was keen on trying the game. The good news, the game plays very fast, it has very easy rules to learn, and the components are very well done. However I feel the game is too simple for my taste. I have to say I played the version without the curses when you reveal a new room. I believe I would like more the game that way because the game gets pretty easy after a couple of runs. The cursed dice is a stroke of genius, this makes the game very cooperative and fun to play as there are a lots of yells to get “un cursed”. I really like this “time pressure” games.

I´m concerned about the replayability to the game, it is fun but I think this is not a game to play often. I feel with more plays it will get old very quickly (As I said before I have only played the basic game and I have not read the rules).

As the game plays so fast you want to play again after each loss :D and that is a good sign.

The theme is ok but nothing that appeals to me.

I believe I will buy this game because it is a great familiar game, but I generally don’t want to play it in my usual gaming sessions, if I want to play something like this I will play Space Alert (a superior game in my book). However I won’t say no to this game as it plays so quickly AND it is fun.

Current Rating: 6.0

RATING: 8.5
- Man do I enjoy this game. Some people don't though, as it can be HECTIC.
- Makes for great fun with 5-6 players grouped round a table, frantically rolling dice and shouting at each other. Then the gong sounds and everyone rushes to get back to the starting chamber. Inevitably someone has a crap roll and gets stuck.. Do you run back to help a mate? How much time do you have? Maybe 10 seconds... Is that enough?
- It's great to see people pull together as a team to help each other through this.
- I think everyone has a great time playing this, but some people find it too stressful and don't want to play anymore after a couple of games.
- I have the big box, which is okay, but really you only need the base game plus one or two of the tricky rooms to add in. We've never played with the Illusions expansion as it just seems too daunting. We also haven't played with the player powers as, even though they look fun, I'm not convinced they're worth the extra rules explanation and thing to remember in the heat of it. Particularly if you only play this once every now and then with a mixture of newbs+experienced players.
- I'm looking forward to exploring the expansion modules, but I won't be too bothered if I never get to, as the game is really fun as is.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Note that I am rating this as a kid's game, as I think the replay value for an adult audience would be very limited.

However, with my 7 year old daughter and 12 year old son, this was a blast. Very tense dice-fest where you continuously roll dice in order to get certain combos that allow you to discover new rooms, move into them, and power up gems that allow you to leave the temple while a 10 minute timer soundtrack plays. You have two mid-game objectives of getting back to the start room that keeps it tense throughout.

The basic game is so simple that I could see lots of modifications to add interest and difficulty as required. Obviously there are a couple of expansions already. But even in the base game you could limit grouping, have gold masks free up less black masks, add to the dice requirements to acquire things. Really, the way this game is designed, it's wide with possibilities. This one had the whole family jumping out of their seats!

RATING: 10
Excellent family co-op game.  Included CD has a 10 minute soundtrack, with cues for when certain gameplay events take place.  Lots of tension, with the soundtrack timer, speed dice rolling, fast discussions, arguments.  Many ways to configure at setup time, and even more if you own the Big Box version or individual Queenie modules.  Can scale difficulty by adjusting the number of gems you have to activate, the number of room tiles in the deck, which rooms appear in the deck (e.g., remove curse rooms to make it easier).  A very fun, unique game experience.  One that I can come back to over and over, because of all the different ways to set it up.  Even with the same setup, the flow of the game can take different turns depending on the order of the room, curse, and treasure tiles, and where they show up on the board.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Lissa won at Queen Games Raffle at Origins 2013.

RATING: 8.5

For my time and money, this equates to a great experience, which never overstays its welcome (even when played 3 or 4 times in a row).  However, it isn't a game I will be thinking about once it's out of my sight.  Great fun though, and it will stay around to keep diversity in the collection.

RATING: 7
Escape is fun.  A lot of fun.  So much fun.

In fact, it's so fun that I almost feel bad for giving it a 7 instead of a 9 or 10.

My biggest problem with Escape is also one of the things I enjoy most about it.  The idea that everyone is working at the same time to ultimately achieve the same goal is really intriguing; but this ultimately starts to falter when you realize how chaotic this gets in a game like this.  Dice are flying everywhere, everyone is incredibly spastic, roll liberties can be (and are often) taken...it just seems to me that if the chaos and panic were reigned in even just slightly, this would be top tier.

The difficulty is against you from the outset, so adding in extra modules CAN certainly increase the fun, but it can also make it even MORE chaotic and add too many things to have to grapple with aside from dice and time.

RATING: 8
Though I don't really like cooperative games at all, Escape has two of my favorite things in games - frantic dice rolling and a soundtrack. IMO soundtracks are not used enough in games - Space Alert and Squad Seven are both great games, and I can't wait for Panicobloc!

That said, my main reservation with Escape is that it's too easy to inadvertently cheat with all of the dice rolling over and over again. I don't care about intentional cheating - that's just silly and I wouldn't even know where to begin. I'm talking more about people making innocent mistakes due to the speed of the game. I guess it doesn't really matter all that much (I still am rating it an 8), but my OCD side finds it bothersome.

I am going to have to keep an eye out for this designer. I also really enjoyed Mammut, though I wish that his games would go to a company other than Queen. The way they've handled the release of the Illusions expansion is really stupid, and I really dislike how they've been using Kickstarter to fund their games.

RATING: 6.5
8.5 to 6.5 - A distraction for the ADHD generation.

Excitement and rush of first impression has been diminished by the fact that though it still gives an adrenalin high you quickly become jaded to the roll-move-repeat mechanic.  I predict you will quickly start looking for other gaming highs.

A realtime collaborative game with CD soundtrack.  Roll dice to escape dungeon.  Though halfway through the game you have to return to your starting point - maybe someone left their coat or purse.

The games strengths are also its weaknesses.

Escape as a collaborative game succeeds because of the limits it sets upon the players.  The most obvious example of a limit being that the designers set is the 10-minute time limit as there is not enough time or 'mental' space in this game for a single player to dominate the direction of the game.  It is a joint rush through the dungeon rather than a follow the leader type of game.  Therefore, everyone will feel involved and an equal part of the outcome.  Furthermore, you can't go off and do your own thing as you need to be together - a person on their own who is cursed is well and truly cursed.  Finally, at the start you only have 5 dice each so you can't be a hero on your own.  Therefore you have a real collaborative game due to the limitations rather than the expansive goals and roles found within some examples of the genre.  Plus with the ten minute time limit, quick rules and quick set-up it will find a space in most game nights.

However, the limits also mean that there isn't much depth or mental engagement in the game. Roll and move, share some dice, roll and move and so on.  With an artificial construct of returning to the starting point meaning you will have to roll and move some more there seems to be an abdication of responsibility by the designers. This may be rectified by expansions but a solution should be in the base game.  There is no gaming logic why they should return to the starting point to just repeat the first few minutes.  Maybe this is rectified in the expansions but this is a lazy design approach.  Maybe the players should have something valuable in the starting tile (as part of the victory condition) which they can't take unless they find certain objects on other tiles.  This would increase the challenge and create a reason for them returning.

In conclusion Escape is fun, frantic, very light, accessible, with great components and has design merit (the positives outweigh the negative design choices) however I do not think it has the substance or enduring quality to be a game you return to again and again.

RATING: 8.7
Type: 1-5 player cooperative timed game of reflexes and dice-rolling.

Best with: 2-4
Weight: Light
Duration: 10 minutes timed
Notes:
time-based dexterity game with dice-chucking
requires interaction and talk to help each other out
some room for dice rolls onto floors or on boards
fully cooperative game
app or mp3-based timer

Players have 10 actual minutes to chuck dice as fast as possible to move around a mysterious temple, discover rooms, unlock chests, find treasure, and reach the exit. Sometimes players are cursed, other times they have dice locked from use, or even get locked in the temple forever if they don't hit certain checkpoints! Oh, and all players are chucking their dice and moving at the same time, as fast as they can.

This game is such sweet fun. You have 10 minutes to work through the temple and get out. This is ridiculously fun, and has just the right amount of interactivity to try and use up crystals, find the exit, and help each other out with locked dice issues.

I also like that this game is easy to teach. While a timed event for a newcomer is stressful, it really just takes one fun run through the game to get what's going on and start making runs that are geared towards success. Throw in some curses like not being able to talk, and you get lots of fun ways to interact with each other while still trying to stay heads-down with your own exploration.

Similar games in my collection: Forbidden Desert (coop game for 2-4)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
10 minutes to teach, 10 minutes to play (and man are those tense minutes!), and it's like popcorn: each game leaves you wanting to play another...which is just fine, since another game only takes 10 minutes! And it's a hoot: chaotic, messy, tense, and above all fun.

There's a lot of luck, but that's fine by me in a short game -- and managing that luck through teamwork and strategy is a key aspect of the game. We played three times on our first time out, trying a different strategy each time; the third time we produced a strategy that led to our first victory -- by a hair.

The components are top-notch, up to Queen's usual high standards. I like that they bundle an expansion with the base game. I love that there are multiple soundtrack options, including downloads from their website. The silent soundtrack is by far the easiest to use, followed by the sand timer. I can't imagine playing with the (much prettier) musical soundtracks -- it's way too fucking hard to hear separate the countdowns and gongs from the music.

RATING: 5.7
I expected this game to be phenomenal. Instead, it is merely good. The greatest advantage of owning this game is its play time. You can knock out several plays in less than an hour, including set up time. Escape is a little light for my taste (in terms of strategy). I do appreciate, however, how the designers have scaled the difficulty. Without the expansions, the game is far too easy for any experienced, adult gamers. With the expansions, there is some tension. Still, I'd simply like the game to be more difficult. We played seven games straight and only lost one because of a stupid mistake. An unfamiliar coop should not play that easily with expansions. I'm excited to try out Escape: Quest though. Hopefully, it will bring more variety/strategy to the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Escape: The Curse of the Temple is an intense, timed, co-op game.  In it players are Indiana Jones-like explorers inside an ancient temple.  It comes with a 10 minute long soundtrack, and when the soundtrack ends the temple collapses on top of anyone who's left in it, and game is over.  So, players have just 10 minutes to search the temple, find enough gems to get out of it, and leave.  The temple itself is a modular board made up of tiles that will be placed out as players discover new rooms.

There are no turns.  As soon as the soundtrack begins everyone starts rolling dice frantically.  The dice are custom 6 sided affairs.  They depict various pictures instead of numbers, or pips.  The co-op aspect of the game comes into play in the sharing of these dice in certain situations.  For example, dice can be lost if the "cursed" side comes up.  Another player can "uncurse" your dice if you've lost too many.  Also, players' combined roll can be used in some rooms to get rid of gems.  Getting rid of gems is important, because to leave the temple players will need to roll 1 "key" more than however many gems are left over.  Everyone must escape for it to be considered a win.

Escape: The Curse of the Temple is pressure filled.  You know you only have 10 minutes, and the soundtrack really ratchets up the sense of near panic.  It starts off slow, but increases in tempo, even featuring a pounding heart-type sound.  The only drawback that I sense is they game does become repetitive after a few plays, as all you're doing every time is rolling dice as fast as you can to get the symbols you need.  It's a good one to play though if you've never played it before, and a really great game to show others.  Watching their reaction if fun!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
First there was Space Alert, which I still consider the essential realtime game despite pretty hardcore learning curve. Now here is Escape, another well-received realtime game. It's way easier to setup and teach. Also, unlike Space Alert, you do the resolutions in realtime aswell while frantically rolling your dice so it feels more lively. Curses are fun too. Sounds pretty perfect so far? Here comes the downside - the replayability is pretty bad. When you've played it ~5 times you'll be winning pretty consistently. 5 games may sound like a lot, but you have to remember that they're 10-minute games. The expansion helped for a while but not in the long run. It's a very fun game and if you haven't played it, I highly recommend it, but its place in a permanent small/medium-sized collection is somewhat problematic. I'm keeping it for memories if not anything else and maybe after couple of years it'll be fun again? But if you are thinking of buying, think twice and play someone elses copy first if possible.

2-Player Comment:
* The more the merrier, but Escape works well with any player count. We play 2p with 12 diamonds.

Expansions:
+Escape: Illusions

RATING: 10
I'll just say it right away: this game is amazing! Mechanically, it's really simple: you roll dice to explore the temple, and when you have activated enough crystals, you can escape. It's cooperative, so everyone works together to escape, and if someone fails, the group loses. The catch is, there's a soundtrack that gives you exactly 10 minutes to do everything. And there are no turns. Everyone rolls their dice as fast as they can. Roll a black mask and you can't reroll that die until you get freed by a golden mask. Get 5 black masks and you're stuck, and will need help to do anything. It's a seriously frantic and fun social experience. Fast set-up and tear down. Works very well both with casual and with experienced players. It's stressful and tense, though. If you want to sit back, relax and think your actions through, this is not the game you want to play. No alpha player problem. No doubt, one of my favorites.

RATING: 7
A great, 10 minutes, stress-filed escape game. The lack of turns and real life count-down genuinely adds to theme of trying to escape and is cleverly built within the dice mechanics.

The need for separating and sticking together makes choices hard, especially when players are locked down and need help. The game only really feels complete with the sound-track, and is certainly not the same without it. A must buy, only if you can handle the tension.

RATING: 4
Game in a Nutshell: Explore a temple in a timed co-op using rapid dice rolling to move, search for treasure, and ultimately escape with your lives.

Played as: 5 player

Pros: It's certainly a different kind of Co-op in that there's zero time to "huddle-up" and come to a consensus once the music starts. There's excitement to the frenzied sound of a table full of people re-rolling dice as fast as possible while shouting needs over the top of it.

Cons: Maybe I just didn't "get it" but at its core it's just a game about rolling and rerolling dice to try and get a certain result. Imagine rolling a handful of dice needing a six... roll, nope, re-roll, nope, re-roll, yep! What's next? A five. Roll, nope, re-roll, and on and on... where others find continued value in this beyond a simple children's game is beyond me. I also think required sound-tracks are bothersome.

Other: I was surprised how solitary my one play felt. It's more about everyone zoning out on their own little dice game in unison with others than a true cooperative experience. For Pete's sake, I played the Escape Experience with 12 different copies of the game going in unison in a small room and wasn't even able to take in the grandness of it all for how into my own "solitaire game" I was.

Best Use: A co-op with a bit of adrenaline edge when the family needs a pick-me-up.

RATING: 8
It happens very rare I come across a game that leaves me completely in love. But boy is this game fun!!

Different setup rules helps determine how hard the challence at defeating the game will be, thus can be ajusted to suit the players abilities.

I dont think the basegame alone will grow stale for the first many games, but it is nice to know that comming expansions will further encrease the possibilities for an even more challinging game, which will help to keep the game fresh as you can mix and match the individual modules as you see fit.

Without hesitation I can declare this beauty an instant classic.

Újrapróbáltuk. A gondom az, hogy nem izgalmas (bár továbbra sem próbáltam az extra dolgokat). A kooperatív játékokban a döntések okozta feszültséget szeretem, itt viszont a kocka általi szerencse dönt, és ez okoz izgalmat. Illetve okozna, mert valamiért egyáltalán nem tudom magam beleélni az omladozó templomból menekülő kalandor bőrébe. RATING: 6.5
In bester Indiana Jones Tradition, versuchen die Spieler in Escape aus einem antiken und verfluchten Majatempel zu entfliehen, bevor dieser über ihnen zusammen bricht. Die Spieler arbeiten dabei zusammen und die Flucht läuft in Echtzeit ab. Im Spiel liegt eine Audio-CD bei, die die dramatische Flucht mit einem 10 Minuten Musikclip untermalt und auch an zwei Stellen ins Spielgeschehen eingreift (durch ein akkustisches Signal). Der Spielverlauf ist recht simpel: Alle Spieler würfeln gleichzeitig und versuchen, wie bei Kniffel, die passenden Symbole zu erwürfeln. Dabei müssen die Spieler in manchen Räumen gleiche Symbole erwürfeln, um diesen zu verlassen. Escape ist ein hektisches Spiel, was als guter Filler oder als Einstieg in einen Spieleabend gut funktioniert.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
An awesome real time dice game where you have 10 minutes to cooperatively explore the temple, brake the curses and escape before the soundtrack runs out.

There is very little to the gameplay here, there's not even a turn sequence- just the start signal goes and everyone starts rolling and shouting and grabbing at their pieces for 10 minutes!

It plays incredibly well though for what it is. Its intense, simple and fun, making it a great short length cooperative game and even a good filler (as long as you have thick walls so your neighbours can't hear you shouting 'I'VE GOT TWO TORCHES!' and 'HELP ME! I'M LOCKED DOWN!!').

I found the game quickly lost its novelty value without the addition of the Curses/Treasures variant. We found after our first two games the base game held no further challenge and we won every time. The Curses/Treasures variant fixes the game and makes it a challenge for adult gamers, although I expect the base game will be enough from a family perspective and casual gamers.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Escape causes you to panic. The game takes place in a "real time" situation, as in the game will always take exactly 10 minutes to complete, win or lose. The soundtrack makes the game too. It's the real cherry on top. My only problem with the game is I find it easy to cheat. I have caught people rerolling dice they shouldn't be able to reroll, and may it be on purpose or not, I would rather loose a fair game than win an unfair one. 

Game does get significantly better with the curse and treasure tiles. The panic and relief these cause fluctuates depending in what you draw and can cause things to go good or bad real fast. Good for experienced players, but makes the game loads of fun.

RATING: 3
The fun of the game comes from all the kinds of problems that emerge from group splitting. However the optimal strategy is to do the exact opposite, forming one big party that tackles triple gem rooms easily, has some use for the spare golden masks from its 15 rolls per second and follows an efficient room exploring pattern:
- 1st pass => east half staying close to the entrance
- 2nd pass => west half staying close to the entrance
- 3rd pass => exit

Once you've figured that out, Escape is unfortunately pretty bland. While it might work as party game with clueless people, cold-blooded fast rollers will have a breeze of a time. The bundled variant tiles raise the difficulty without adding any meaningful challenge. Perhaps a further expansion has figured that out and given incentives for the group to split, but that probably means replacing most tiles of the base game, which is already quite expensive thanks to Queen Games' usual pricing policy.

Then there's the real time component, which I love in theory, but doesn't work because of golden masks, often leading to multiple people unlocking black dice when someone says "I can unfreeze 3." Little approximations that can hardly be checked because everyone is busy rolling and shouting simultaneously, resulting in a lot of gentle and unintentional cheating.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
In this real time game, players have 10 minutes to escape from a collapsing temple. Players are continuously rolling dice to either: explore a new tile, discover a new tile, activating gems, or rolling to escape. The dice also have black symbols, which make the die useless, but can be recovered by rolling a gold symbol, which reactivates two black dice. Players can escape when they have activated enough gems so that the escape roll is manageable.

This is a frenetic dice rolling game, since you have to go back to the start chamber a couple of times during the game, otherwise you lose a die. Teamwork is essential, since some players can roll too many black dice, and need help to get out. 

It's fun, having played the basic game, the curses module, along with the treasures module. I'm looking forward to more plays. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Fun, silly, simplistic, chaotic.

I wouldn't suggest this to someone that purely likes strategic games, as this game is so fast paced and crazy that strategy is generally thrown out the window for quick thinking, gut instinct, and decent luck. 

It's a co-op game that generally avoids quarterbacking, mainly because the quarterback is too busy and too under pressure to make decisions for everyone in the group.

It is interesting how some groups may decide to stick together to share golden masks (and therefore keep all of their dice in use), but some other groups I play with like to split up and explore large parts of the temple in  a short time span.

The game, for only being 10 minutes long, certainly finds a way to make sure those entire 10 minutes are filled with maximum intensity. 

I'm generally someone who's into something a bit more... thinky? (as pretentious as that sounds), but escape is one of those games I've played quite a bit, for quite a while, and it still hasn't gotten less fun.

RATING: 6
Simple concept, chaotic gameplay, raucous fun, but despite its size, it is basically a filler. Interest in Escape is like a flash-fire; burning brightly, but for a very short duration.

E:tCotT's extremely short play length may increase its entertainment half-life, but only in number of plays, overall time spent with it will likely be very brief. The Curses and Treasures module[s?] included will likely get just a single play, because they don't change what the game is, rather they just add unnecessary complexity.

Escape may be too difficult to win with any regularity. For the amount of gems needed to escape there are just too many useless empty rooms in the draw pile. Replacing them with the tiles from the Treasures module might ameliorate the problem.

The biggest issue I have with Escape is the soundtrack. The gongs aren't audible enough. I wish there was just a person who said "Explore, Run, Explore, Run, Explore and Escape". That would be far more clear.

Escape is the sort of fun, cooperative experience that is just right for introducing boardgames to those that have never.

RATING: 6
I'm mixed on this one, I like that it only lasts 10 min.  The game does instill a frantic feeling and gets your heart racing which is cool. The components are nice, maybe too nice (expensive) for such a simple game.  Its so chaotic with everyone talking over each other that it is easy to miss sound cues.  Also you are on the honor system as to your rolls which, at least it is a co-op so it works.  It works better as the warm up than cool down game of the night because after a night of gaming it just seems exhausting to play.  The game has deliberately short playtime and you see most if not all of the tiles each time, this makes repeated plays unappealing, yet you need to play with the same group enough to toss in the curses and treasures in which is just more chaos and requires you to memorize the symbols on the cards. YMMV.

RATING: 8.5

RATING: 8
This game is intense, loud and FUN! I took two copies of this game to a gaming group that consisted of twelve kids 11 to 15 years of age. They played with five players at each board and I played the sound track over the classroom PA system. Wow! Talk about intensity and excitement!  Yelling, laughing, cursing (I asked them keep that to a minimum) and profuse sweating was the course of the afternoon.  Since each game only lasts ten minutes, they were able to rotate in the left out kids frequently. Some were glad to be out to rest. They played this game (two simultaneous games actually) for the entire hour and a half!  They loved, loved, LOVED this game! 

For as much as that particular group loved the game, it is too intense for some.  I played with a smaller group of kids at my house (two boys, two girls; all aged from 11 to 12; one was my daughter).  Sure enough the intensity was just as high as with the older kids, but at the end of the ten minute game, one of the boys began to cry.  It was way too intense for this sensitive little guy.  I quietly put the game away and got out Stone Age, which he and the others loved.

For many, this game is loads of loud, intense fun.  But there are those that prefer something a little quieter and cerebral.  In spite of this caveat, you should have this game in your collection!

RATING: 9.5
Intensely Intense game! This is a fun party game. The intensity of trying to escape the temple is heart felt by all players. The base game is difficult in and of itself. Add with the treasures, it still is difficult, add in the cursed tiles and the difficulty increases even more. So far, with our first play with a group of non-gamers at a party, the immediately discovered that a 6th player was necessary because of all the people having a great time. My wife joined in with the 6th player equipment from the illusions expansion immediately. This game is so well balanced and the components are top top quality. At first I thought this game is so hard, when will I need any of the expansions. After a few plays we became ready for more, adding in the treasures...and more, adding in the cursed tiles and 6th player. Everyone loved this game! As my wife was playing with a group and intensely trying her hardest to get back to the entrance before the doors slammed shut. I whispered in her ear that this may be one of the best party games ever! She couldn't speak at the time, but later she agreed! One of the best moments of the game was when one player playing her second game, screamed "Get Back...Get Back everyone!" just before the doors slammed shut. 

Some great elements of the game are losing a die because you cannot get back to the entry room in time and the opportunity to give someone one of your dice when you safely leave the temple. You are passing a bit of equipment on to a fellow adventurer to help them get to safety. Also, helping each other gain enough dice for collecting gems in the gem rooms is a sweet bit of cooperative play.

RATING: 7
心得:
比逃離喪屍好玩些
感覺蠻需要合作的
且可以SOLO
遊戲重點是快速判斷要留那些骰使用那些骰啟動
使用了擴充之後最好能優先解決擾人的詛咒
不過基本上還是運氣很重要的遊戲
規則:
*起始板塊放中間，出口外洗勻抽兩個放起始板塊兩側，抽四個跟出口板塊洗勻放板塊堆下面(1~2人時把出口插在中間)，根據人數1~2/3/4/5人時放7/11/14/16顆寶石在寶石板塊上，下面再額外放兩顆
*每個人拿五顆骰(1人七顆)跟一個顏色米寶放中間，一個顏色標記放面前
*遊戲根據音樂進行10分鐘，逃出獲勝，遊戲開始就可以不斷擲骰
*板塊右下角為進入該板塊要花的骰面，中間為拿寶石要花的骰面，放板塊是要出口相連，黑色入口則是一開始打開時要用來跟目前的任一個入口相連
*骰子不斷重骰並保留想要的骰面，黑色不行，黃色可解除兩顆黑色，同樣位置可幫解除，執行行動後用過的要全部重骰，保留的也可重骰
1.進入板塊 使用對應骰面進入該相鄰有入口的板塊
2.發現板塊 兩個綠色面且有出口沒連的可拿一個新板塊來相連
3.啟動魔法祭壇 骰出對應骰面 放一顆寶石到祭壇，可多人合作，多個祭壇的只能完成一個
4.逃跑 在出口骰出等於剩餘寶石數加1的藍色面，逃出後可把一顆骰給隊友
5.可把寶石圖板外的一顆寶石放進寶石圖板來讓所有人重骰黑色骰面
*停到銅鑼聲時要在時限內回到起始板塊，否則會少一顆骰
***模組1跟2**
*使用新的13個版塊擋開出的版塊有神像拿一個詛咒版塊，獲得詛咒效果可單獨擲骰解決
*有寶藏就放寶藏，擲出結果可拿，都是一次性效果

RATING: N/A
密室脫逃：受詛咒的神廟
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Frantic dice rolling fun for those who like frantic dice rolling fun. Count me one. You've got one eye on your dice, rolling and re-rolling to explore for new rooms (roll 2 greens next to an open door), enter a room (roll the entrance combo) or acquire gems (roll keys) in the gem rooms. At the same time, you're keeping an eye on all the other players, talking and agreeing what you'll do together, because if you're together you can help each other out getting rid of any black results you roll (which lock those dice away) and also combining rolls of keys to get gems. At the third and two-thirds points, as gonged out by the 10 minute soundtrack that you play within, you need to race back to the start so that you don't lose a die. Or do you just cop it and keep going? 10 minutes just flies. It's not easy, it takes practice to win, which is a good thing. It won't be easy to get to the table with non-gamers because frantic dice-rolling usually isn't everyone's cup of tea, and it's not going to sit well with studious euro-gamers, but there's a bunch of people in between who will enjoy the ride and the co-op strategising on the fly. As meaty a 10 minute filler as you can find.
