RATING: 8
"Frantic dice-chucking real-time co-op. Great theme, and requires actual cooperation. Even after over a dozen plays, I prefer it without the expansions. I wish the soundtracks had less extraneous noise and clearer meaningful signals."

What I like:
- Co-op with actual cooperation, and no "boss players"
- Quick to teach, quick to play, fun
- Nice components

What I don't like:
- It's pretty easy to accidentally cheat
- There are too many curse tiles in the expansion
- Soundtrack might not work in all venues, and a sand timer is a poor substitute

For me, I would want to play the basic tiles at least 5-10 times before adding the curse/treasure or other expansions. I didn't have the basic rules down, and the curses and treasures just added a bit too much and overwhelmed me. After the base game is second nature, I think adding the other tiles for variety would be good.

RATING: 5
This game combines three things I'm not a fan of: cooperative play, Yahtzee-style dice-rolling, and time limits.  You roll dice, using the symbols you roll to move around and complete challenges (often needing others to help you with the challenges), while frantic music plays in the background.  If you roll a certain side on your dice, then your character can get stuck, and you need to get other players to come help you by rolling another symbol.  If you like frantic dice-rolling mayhem, then you may enjoy this.  I don't.

(3 plays)

RATING: 7
Escape: The Curse of the Temple is a light, innovative, real-time tile laying game in which you are trying to escape an ancient temple before the exit is sealed shut, trapping your intrepid adventurer forever. The 10 minute soundtrack keeps the players on task while they frantically roll dice to discover new rooms, unlock the mysteries of the cursed gems, and try to crack the lock on the exit. 

The game play is, as you might imagine, fast paced and breathtaking. There is no downtime here! Well, until one of your dice goes careening off the table and you waste that last few precious seconds to find it! 

The base game is a good introduction to the game play, but does tend to be rather easy. For an intermediate level game, I will mix half of the base game tiles with half of the Curses and Treasures expansion, which comes with newer editions. For a more challenging experience, go all in with the Curses and Treasures - and then add some extra gems! 

The one minor criticism I have is with the soundtracks. A number of soundtracks are available on the website. My favorites provide a rich tapestry of background effects that really enhance the mood. Unfortunately, the level of the background effects is too high for me to easily hear the gongs (timer cues), so I'm stuck listening to the soundtrack versions with no sound effects, just the timer cues. 

A note on set-up: The instructions suggest for a solo game to insert the exit tile somewhere in the middle of the tile stack. This makes for a game that is far too short. Instead, set up just like for multiplayer games by shuffling the exit tile with the top four tiles of the tile stack and then putting them on the bottom.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Quick, fast fun even solo!

This game is just plain fun.  It is rare that a board game gets your heart pumping but this one does because you and your friends have to escape from the temple together before the timer runs out.

A nice feature of the game is the you can play on your own or with a total of 5 players.  The game scales nicely although in my experience the game seems to get harder with more players because there needs to be more cooperation and negotiation.

That's because in this game everyone plays together.  To win everyone has to exit the temple before the time runs out or everyone loses - trapped underground forever.

The game mechanics are really simple to teach which is another major plus.  You just roll a few dice and the symbols tell you what you can do.

There is no waiting time.  Everyone plays at the same time which creates a sense of drama and chaos which is not felt in many other games where you have to wait your turn to play.

Finally, the game is short. 10 minutes.  This explains why you can play so many in a game night and why it has been the most played game of the holidays.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I think this is a great game. It has an interesting concept, the theme really shines in this game, it's very simple, and it's quick.

The dice and tiles are good quality, and it's always satisfying to place one of the large tiles when you explore a new room. Players are under constant, and usually pretty heavy stress because this game is time based. The game is a co-op, but it's co-op elements are a bit ignorable. If you roll blacks masks on the dice, then you can't reroll those dice, and if all of your dice are black masks then a friend must come in to give you some gold masks to negate the black mask effects. Also, there are times where you're supposed to roll a certain number of dice (like, 7 torches) in order to get a lot of gems, and your friends can help with that, but otherwise there's really not a lot of cooperation going on. The game is too hectic to really talk things out in grand detail, but this isn't really a negative point because grand detail isn't exactly needed to think your way out of this game.

The game only lasts 10 minutes, and it may make it seem like an experienced group could blast through this game quickly without a real moment of any suspense, but there are suspense moments about every 2 and half minutes where everyone must return to the starting tile in about a minute or else they'll lose a die. There's a lot of opportunity for scares, fun, and cooperation to help someone make their way back as the music amps up, the heatbeat sound begins, and you know there's only seconds to get them back to safety.

Overall, I'd suggest this game somewhat highly. It's lack of strategic depth may make it's replay value somewhat low after the "new game high" settles down, but it's something I'd always be willing to play just because of how quick the setup is and how quick the game is to play.

RATING: 7.7
Roll dice Roll dice roll dice, repeat for ten minutes or less.  I've only played solo with the base game and the first two modules.  This game is a very unique experience.  It can be tense since it is real time and you must know the rules before playing because there is no real pause in the game. Luckily it is a very simple system to pick up.  I think the game simulates its theme quite well and almost has a video game feel to it. Unfortunately it odes seem to lack with replay value as it feels so same-y each time you play.  I suspect once you add the expansions this might not be the case.  I suspect this game shines more with 2 or more rather than a solo as the player interaction is a key element of the fun of this so I hope I can try that out someday.

RATING: 10
Note that this is a 10 thanks to the huge amount of content I have for it. Without the expansions (particularly Quest) it would be around 7. Good, but not beyond entry level. The concept of the soundtrack is awesome, and the curses & treasures are a good start, but it's the quests, character powers, illusions and special chambers (in that order) that make each game so different and enjoyable. I've also had a LOT of fun with this one solo, but that requires a fair amount of house ruling.

If there are any down-sides... maybe resetting the tile deck, and the fact that most people won't want to play this more than a few times in a row (and it takes a while to build them up to the really cool modules).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I'm not usually one for hectic games full of confusion - Galaxy Trucker is usually my limit, but the idea of a 10 minute dice fest I could play with the kids attracted me to Kickstarting this. The eight year old finds it too hectic (Puerto Rico is more her thing), the five year old thinks it's great (his favourite games are Lancaster and The Castles of Burgundy). Both could be roped into more games easily enough. The curse tiles are particularly appealing to them. The wife hates cooperative games (her favourite game is El Grande), but merely dislikes this one. Me? It's better than I thought it would be and is a peg that suits a suitable hole in my collection.

The box is packed full of value. You've got your 13 starting chambers for a basic game. When you've conquered that you can ramp up the difficulty by adding more gems to the pot. Crank the complexity up a notch by substituting the base chambers for the curse chambers and you'll find yourself doing things like losing dice that fall on the floor, playing with one hand or playing in silence until the curses are broken.

Players are in constant discussion, but unlike Pandemic and other co-operative games there's extreme time pressure. The dominating player has no place here - all players will need help and really work as a team to succeed. It's a stressful game, and if you play to unwind and  relax then you might want to avoid this because by the time the ten minutes is up you'll need a few minutes to chill and sit back in your seat.

Good fun, but they really hit the nail on the head with the ten minute time limit. I see this hitting the table often as a filler and it's very welcome to do so.

What a crazy riot this game is! Our family played it a ton our first weekend with it, and my kids especially really loved it.

My almost-14-year-old son describes this as his favorite game because there is no down time, turns are fast, and the game doesn't last too long. After playing the basic game and then introducing the curse cards, my 12-year-old son said we should think of our own curses to add on. And my 7-year-old son quickly caught on, plus he is good at making sure he shares his golden masks to un-curse dice.

But really, it's just chaotic fun. I didn't realize how intense it might get. And my kids think just because they escape and I am still in there trying to roll 2 more keys, they don't lose. (But I can't think of a thematic reason to convince them otherwise.) We'll be playing this game a lot at my house.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 4.5
10 minutes of rolling dice and screaming and trying to work together and rolling the dice really really fast and crying for help and absolutely no breathing. We had a lot to do even without the added "expansions", so I don't think replayabilty will be a huge problem, but it's not one of those games one would play the whole evening anyway.

RATING: 6.5
This is definitely a fun game. It involves A LOT of frantic dice rolling with a good dose of player interaction and sometimes confusion thrown in.  That combination makes for some tense games and good times.  There is nothing really deep or complex, but that's fine for what it is.  The game plays in only 10 minutes each time and seems to be a win with box regular gamers as well as non-gamer friends and family. I was skeptical about this game at first, but after playing it with my regular group a few times I decided that I had to get it and have since really enjoyed the solo play.

SOLO PLAY:  Escape: The Curse of the Temple is another cooperative game that can be played solo. However, this one is all about rolling dice and is filled with tension and excitement. The game isn't overly complex, but there are various ways to increase the difficulty as well as additional modules to increase the variety.

RATING: 6
Real tough one to rate as I do like a good dice roller... But still not sure about this.

Findings after a solo run through and 4P game

Things I like:

 - Dice
 - Quick play
 - Modular board
 - Component quality (as with most Queen releases)

Things I don't like:

 - Easy to get 'locked out' of rolls so you're stranded waiting for help
 - Due to time constraints have seen on more than one occasion players mistake die rolls an take rooms etc with wrong rolls.
 - Due to time constraints it's impossible to (even quickly) refer to the rule book if we have queries during game play.
 - Soundtrack that come with the game.

RATING: 6
Collective relentless rolling. Roll. Roll. Roll. Roll. Roll.  Hey can someone help me out here so that I can roll more. Roll. Roll. Roll. Roll.

I guess that there are a number of tiny micro-decisions. Mostly, I felt that you were just along for the ride, and then you see what the results are.

I will say that the soundtrack sucks. We had a difficult time determining the warning for the gong and the gong itself.  It could have just used a sand timer.

I question the re-playability of the game.  The modular board ultimately feels insignificant, what does it really matter which order the tiles come out in and what shape the map has, especially when everyone just moves around in a pack.  OK everyone go in this direction, when the gong warning comes up, turn around to get to the center and go the other way, you will hit the exit no matter what direction you go in if you all stay together.

[b]--- Summary ---[/b]
Players each have their own set of dice. The board consists of a few starting tiles; a pile of other tiles are nearby, face down. Players simultaneously roll their dice, trying to come to whatever combination is necessary to accomplish the task on the tile (explore a new tile, collect a gem, move to a new tile, etc.). Players may allow each other to use any of their rolls, but only if their meeples are in the same room (tile). One side of each d6 is a skull -- the die stays locked if a skull is rolled (the other dice may be rerolled freely). Must spend one gold die to unlock up to 2 locked dice.

The game is played with a (10-minute?) timer. During that time, they must return to the starting tile once. They must also collect a certain number of gems and then escape back out of the temple.

I completely dismissed it when it was on Kickstarter as a game with not enough meat, even "kiddie", and what I heard and saw of it after release didn't change my opinion.  A friend in my regular game group brought it by though and for that price I'll at least try it out.

I still won't buy it myself because I don't think it has a long shelf life but I enjoyed it.  The tension of games played in real-time really adds a great dynamic to games that might otherwise not be very fun.  The decision tree for this game isn't very large but when added to the stress of time constraints become your world for a few seconds.  Your friend needs help because he has 5 black masks but you already collected 4 keys needed for those gems and you need to head back to start soon aaaahhhh!!!!

In the end though I have to agree with my original assessment.  The game is simple and just doesn't have enough meat on it for me to last more than a few plays.  And it does seem "kiddie", it is a game you can teach and play with children and doesn't offer enough to hold the interest of adults who are after more like me.  I did have fun with it and I will play if someone asks because for those ten minutes your adrenaline is pumping and you're having a great time.  I just think that feeling ends after a few plays, especially if in succession.

Also, as a disclaimer, the game is a dice-fest and completely random.  Our first game we smashed it, collecting enough gems to get out easily early, all getting back to start in time twice, finding the exit, and winning with 1:00+ left on the clock.  Second game we were murdered, all constantly rolling 3-5 black masks, not getting the symbols to move into the next room let alone collect the gems, losing dice during both closures, and ending the game nowhere near having a chance of winning.  I like that (to a certain extent) but what I just described sounds like hell for a lot of people.  Full disclosure, we did play with the curse tiles the second game which added some difficulty but the majority of why we lost had nothing to do with those tiles and more to do with just horrible luck with our rolls.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

What fun :) Played 3 games this evening. Lots of shouting!

RATING: 5
Cooperative real-time Yahtzee: roll the right symbols to do actions (like move into a room or place crystals); some actions might need 10 of a given symbol, requiring multiple players in the same room to cooperate.

It's like Space Alert for non-gamers -- it's got the time pressure, but not the same degree of cooperation or decision-making. (In fairness, the expansions do seem to add a little depth; in future I would not play without at least the curses.) 

Not bad, good even, but not enough to it to grab me: I like games with difficult decisions and Escape doesn't have any at all. Unlike Space Alert, there's also a pretty good chance you'll feel like you failed just because you rolled poorly, rather than any failure of planning or communication, and I hate that.

I might still be inclined to break it out as a quick filler, but the somewhat onerous setup requirements with the CD make that infeasible.

RATING: 4
An enticing and original concept: a real-time dice game.

However, in practice the game doesn't quite work. The real-time aspect means that the game almost needs a referee/GM to work properly. There's no time to answer rules questions or spot mistakes once the game has started (e.g. we had players picking up black dice, moving through walls, moving the wrong playing piece by mistake). The need for the soundtrack also makes the game difficult to play in the kind of communal spaces that most gaming clubs happen in (pubs etc). Traded away in June 2014. Likely will not play again.

RATING: 9
Reduce because, without expansions, it can get very samey.

CAUTION:  For those of you serious gamers who have forgotten that games should be fun, don't bother with this game.  It is explosively fun and should best be left alone if your raison d'être is to show how massive your brain is.  

In my opinion, however, this is the best game of the last few years!  Seriously fun and heart pounding!  I can't see other games the same way any more... 

I can see this working in almost any game group and with ages probably from 7 (minimum) on up.

Waiting for so many more varieties of this same mechanic.  Dungeon runs, mazes, clowns, space ships, zombies (of course), war games...

I'm sure this, or something like it, will be found in Walmart, I predict, by maybe 2018 or so.

An unwavering 10! 

ALSO:  Just played it with my wife and daughter six times in a row.  My daughter said: "This game is awesome!"  She was waving her hands around and looked like she was crying and laughing at the same time.  Never has a game had this reaction from my family.  Never...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The curses are really fun and the way they affect the real world is something you don't often see in a game (players have to hold a hand on their head, etc.). Because of the soundtrack and the time limit, you really feel the pressure to move through the temple.

Update: Still liking it. The difficulty here is something that I think every co-op game should incorporate: you can usually win the game on the normal difficulty setting. This means that you can have fun and be confident of a win with new players, then increase the difficulty as you wish. Some co-op games just seem hopeless, like Ghost Stories, even on their lowest difficulty setting. Can't wait to try it with the new expansions that will be coming out.

Update again: The Quest expansion and the designer's new recommended setup are now essential for this game. The quests make it more difficult and now change up the strategy quite a bit, while the characters help balance out the difficulty a little and just make the game much more fun.
Previous to this expansion, we would commonly just move one way from the beginning, sticking together, then after the first gong we would explore out from the other side of the start tile. Now with Quest, you want to spread out a little to try to find the quest tile and beat them early so you can escape before time runs out. With Quest, this went from a good game to a great one.

Sold, replaced with the Escape Big Box.

RATING: 6.9
Real time games aren't really my thing and snap decisions aren't my forte. So I was a little nervous about whether this game would break me. But the decisions in this game aren't really that deep, so there's never a time when you need to invest much thought into them.

But that also means that the fun part of this game probably isn't going to be in making interesting decisions. And it's not. What's fun about the game is the hectic scramble. Rolling, rolling, rolling, shouting and screaming. Desperately trying to get stuff done before you get completely hosed.

I found the game fun for what it was... a short filler game. We ended up playing five times in a row and by the end I was getting burned out on the game, but for a filler and just a play or two, it's great.

1:The high stress nature of the game can be off putting for some people who arent fast acting.

RATING: 8
This is an interesting and unique game that is unlike anything I've played before.  The title is accurate - it really makes you feel like you're rushing to get out of a cursed temple.  The soundtrack is a brilliant addition to the game.  There are definite moments of excellent tension when someone is locked and you need to rescue them before time runs out, and you really do need to rely on each other to do well so it easily builds a sense of comradery.  It is easy for a group to become too good at the game after a few plays though, and if a group is too good then there is no tension.  The curses and treasures module really helps with this problem though.  It's a fun one to pull out every once in a while, but there isn't enough meat there to warrant a super high rating.

RATING: 6
Escape plays like a co-op, more elaborate version of Shark Attack!, in that it involves realtime dice throwing on a timer. Because of this mechanic, gameplay is a little chaotic and quite intense, making me question its replayability in the long run. Consequently, I am not always in the mood to play it. RATING: 9
Very enjoyable real-time co-op. Most players are polarized by the hectic real-time aspect, but the ones that like it really like it. Curses like "can't talk" or "one hand stuck to your head" force you to improvise in ways other games don't.

Fun, easy to explain and set up, and most people are willing to try it when they find it only takes 10 minutes to play.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
One of a handful of real time board games in my collection, Escape's Norwegian designer, Ostby is slowly climbing up my ladder of notable new designers in the Euro game genre. Both his games thus far, Escape and Mammut have been quite unique in game play while his third creation I have played, Hotel Samoa, was just mediocre. In Escape, players roll five dice simultaneously and as many times as needed to advance their avatars around a maze of tiles as they try to escape a cursed temple that is about to collapse. Using a sound track ala Space Alert to mark the passage of time, players have to cooperate to unlock specific activation sites to capture gems which will facilitate the final escape at the exit. All players will race against time to unlock as many gems as possible without getting trap in the temple at the end of 10 minutes. There is plenty of frantic die rolling coupled with lots of incoherent chatter among players. This game has shades of Ligretto Dice crossed with Space Alert and while it breaks no new ground, the game play is certainly unique enough that it warrants a place in any collection that prizes novelty. One thing of note, the base game itself is quite challenging that with the expansions and additional hazards, the game must be quite daunting and brutal. Playing a few times with a similar group of friends will greatly help in communication.

RATING: 8.7
This game is fun at all player counts.  It's wild and crazy with 4 and 5 with everyone talking over top each other trying to get things done.  It's a little less wild with 3-4, but no less fun.  With 2 players it is calmer, not as loud, but my husband and I still have fun.  With 2 players, it seems like it's easier to add all the expansions in to see how they work together.  Gives me the feeling I have more time to get things done. 

 If we haven't made it out of the temple after a couple tries and everyone else it ready to stop, I have even had fun playing solo to see if I can make it out of the temple alive.  

You can teach the base game to anyone and they will learn it quickly.  More experienced gamers will probably want to add in more of the expansions to make it more challenging.

RATING: 7
The short of it is that this game is just straight up fun to play.  It's frantic and tense, and it has everyone shouting around the table ("Does [i]any[/i]one have any yellow masks?") trying to maintain the chaos that's threatening to bring the temple down on top of you.  Sure, it's a little prone to luck, but all of the game's moving parts come together in a game that's a bit more experience than game, but still leaves you with a sense of satisfaction once it's over.  My only issue is that the atmospheric tracks can be a little unclear the first few times you play, but there is a track on the website that removes all the incidental parts of the track so you can know when things are happening.

2 plays: 4 players
3 plays: 5 players

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I had backed this on Kickstarter, but ended up selling it with the expectation that I wouldn't play it much, and after playing it once that was a good decision. *However*, it is a pretty great game, one I would never turn down.

The basic premise is you (and 2 to 4 of your friends) are stuck in a temple and need to get out in 10 minutes. You'll discover new rooms, move between rooms, place gems in rooms to appease the temple, and eventually escape. And you'll do all of this by rolling dice as fast as possible because **Escape** is played in real-time. You can roll your dice as much as you want, but you'll eventually roll dice that can't be re-rolled unless you get another die face to "unlock" them. It's possible to be completely locked, in which case you'll need a friend to come over and help you out, so it's best to not completely split the party (but you knew that already).

In my one play, we had a full compliment of 5 players and the game hummed along. The soundtrack did it's job of making us even more tense than we otherwise were and the 10 minute timer is absolutely perfect, this game *can't* overstay it's welcome.

So why am I glad I didn't buy it? It's a fun game, but it's one I would only get played in groups and I have so many other games to play with larger groups.

RATING: 7
This cooperative dice-a-thon far outshines [i]D-Day Dice[/i], as there are actual decisions regarding collaboration and splitting up the party.  My suggestion is to play the basic game only once, as the curse cards (I put my hand where?) are truly enjoyable.

[i]Space Alert[/i] is also a great timer-driven game, but its advertised 10-minute playtime is off the mark due to the post-soundtrack game resolution.  [i]The Curse of the Temple[/i], on the other hand, is literally only 10 minutes long.  My kids and Ameritrash-friendly gaming groups are sure to get a big kick out of this one.

RATING: 7
This is a pretty enjoyable cooperative game.  Easy to learn and easy to play.  My issue with the game is trying to keep your dice rolls straight.  I assume that there are a lot of mistakes made by players throughout the game.  That is, keeping track of what was rolled, what dice were used, what you still need, etc.  The fast pace of the game invites these kinds of errors.  Even with this minor flaw, it is a fun game to bring out especially for newbees.  It is notable that some people do not like the stressful fast pace of this game.  One of our gamer friends will not play it for that reason.  It gets her heart racing and she does not enjoy that aspect of the game.  That's the part I love.

RATING: 6.5
10 minutes of pure chaos, plain and simple. It only really lends itself to a couple plays in an evening, but it's great when you don't have a ton of time to play something, want to just have some goofy fun with friends, or want a quick filler between other games.

The game devolves down to frantically rolling dice, screaming to other people what we should be doing as a team to escape the temple all while having this creepy soundtrack playing in the background that is dictating the pace of the game and acting as the games timer.

More or less a dexterity dice-rolling heart-attack inducer than anything else. Strategy is all but thrown out the window as you are essentially herding cats through a burning building.

I haven't played this game in a long time but is something that I'd like to get back to the table again soon. It's nice to play some games once and a while where it's more about the experience than winning or losing the game.

RATING: 10
Escape is easily one of the most enjoyable and tense games I have played in ages. I absolutely adore it!

I never thought I could enjoy a real-time game so much, especially with a soundtrack gimmick, but it just works, and works incredibly well. The game also scales well and works equally well at all player counts.

After 15 plays I have yet to tire of this game. I have also not introduced it to anyone that hasn't loved it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.2
We’ve never played a real-time game before this one. We’ve looked to this one before, but it could never convince us to buy it. Then we bumped into a very nice offer, which could convince us to “buy before we try”. Very little time we have to play a boardgame these days, but last night we managed to find some time. Setting up the game will take about 10 minutes (well, if you placed everything in zip-bags like we did). Playing the game will also take 10 minutes. Not a single second more.  One thing we hated about this game, was the huge amount of noise it was generating at a convention like Spiel last year. The solution from the publisher is that they have placed a sandtimer inside the box, so man wouldn’t need to play a CD. But we were at home, instead of an convention, so we used the soundtrack provided. And to be honest, the amount of tension the creepy music is creating is huge. The tension which there is, is the magic of the game. Not the mechanism, that’s just rolling dice like a mad man, until you’ve rolled the right combination. Is this a fun game to play? Yes, it is. And that is something we didn’t expect that we would say. Don’t expect a deep game, this is a party game. But it is a party game, which is different. No strange questions are asked. No knowledge is required. You won’t have to do weird things. Just roll the dice. Work together to get rid of the gems, and escape…..

RATING: N/A
Absolutely frantic, but fantastically themed. The soundtrack adds so much depth to the game, leaving everyone panicked and distraught by the end. 
It's very simple to alter the difficulty level of the game, either by A) adding more gems, or B) adding in other "useless tiles" or even the dreaded C) You don't start with the "start" tile on the board. You have to find it before the first gong. 
(I don't recommend C unless you are masochistic.)

RATING: 6
This game is wacky.  Roll dice at warp speed and try real hard not to accidentally cheat.  There's a lot to keep track of: don't reroll black masks, gold masks let you reroll 2 black masks, you can give gold masks to coplayers who share a room with you, how many keys do you need to escape, do you have to have a hand on your head, are your gold masks nerfed by a curse, listen for the gongs and know how far you are from the starting room, and on and on, all in real time.
